< Review>
This place was great! This will be our new go to pumpkin patch! Lots of land and stuff to do (even during covid). Everything was very reasonable priced, pumpkins were $2.50-$10. Activities were included or nicely priced compared to others in the areas around us! Go support locals! Especially ones who are not trying to price gouge you!<//Review>

Lots of help even with Covid 19. The employees are all very helpful and get you through the selection, paying and tree prep quickly. And despite the huge demand for trees this year we were still able to find a couple types of really nice 6 to 8 foot precuts in enough quantity to have the I like this one but I like that one kid discussion. :)  was well distanced, honored needs for masks and again were very efficient and helpful. In a hard year, was the break we needed and this place never fails to provide it. Love also supporting local family business and purchase yearly hand made ornament for the tree. Looking forward to next when the fire and hot drinks are bad too!< /text>

<review>Nuh-uh. Not this Starbucks. I'm sorry, but just, NOPE.

I was so excited when it first opened up. The other Starbucks was half hour walk away. When you have no car to drive, and when you love Starbucks as much as me, you'll understand how excited I was.

However, the drinks were just awful! Maybe it's because the staffs are all new? First, they gave me extra ice when I asked for light ice. I asked them to change it, but they just scooped out all the ice, and left the rest of the cup empty. They offered an explanation before I could point out the empty space. "Sorry, if I add more milk, it'll taste bad." Okay, fine, I'll just drink my half cup of mocha when I payed for the price of one.

Few days later, a friend asked me to bring her a cup of latte macchiato. I also got myself a cup of the mango dragonfruit drink. When she got her drink, it just tasted like heavy creamer and milk. There was absolutely no flavor in it other wise. Sadly, we had to throw the whole cup away. I drank my mango dragonfruit, but it was very watered down, and I think they forgot about the mango syrup...

Few months later (a week or two weeks ago), I thought they had enough time to learn, so I went and visited again. I got myself a cup of white chocolate mocha. Ugh... It looked just like milk (yes, pain white), and taste just like milk.... I asked the server about it, and she kindly remade my drink. "With extra pump of white mocha," she says. Only, this time it was so sweet, the mocha and chocolate flavor was way too much. Well, it's better than the milk...

It's going to be another few months before I come back. Hopefully, they'll be real Starbucks by then... Hopefully...</review>< pics>

<Text>We were introduced to this place by a colleague from work. He raved about their food and so I brought my office staff for a treat. We all loved the food! But when we had the chance to discuss our experience in terms of service, we all agreed that the Mother, Pina (the main cook) and her daughter, the server did not treat us well. They were friendly to other customers who were white but noticeably different with us. Because of their good food, our first not pleasant experience did not stop us from coming back. On our next visit my children who are Italian food lovers joined me and my office crew. It was again pretty obvious that while the daughter and server was very chatty with other white customers, she was hardly talking to us and forgetting our orders and needed to be followed up. We did try to be friendly guests but for some reason, we as a group, were not appealing to them. When kitchen is not so busy, Pina would get out and talk to customers but not to us. Not taking offense to our experiences, we patronized them 2 more times by ordering party trays but even these were not a good experience. We stopped patronizing Pina's since then. There are other well deserving restaurants out there.I don't want to name our bad experiences but you can read between the lines and determine for yourself.</Text>< rating>

< Text>
Polo Lounge isn't just a place to eat, it's a place to BE. Not just a lounge, but a tradition that dates back decades to the glory days of Old Hollywood. Yes, the food is awesome, the staff are warm and friendly, and it is a beautiful setting. But it's much more. You never know what old familiar faces you might see there. This is our favorite place to escape in Beverly Hills. I prefer table # 3 where Frank Sinatra used to sit when he and Barbara lived just around the corner on Foothill. You can see everybody coming in from there, which is exactly why he liked it! There are many great little cafes and high profile restaurants to eat in 90210, but Polo Lounge will forever be in a class by itself.</Text>

<Text>If you want the LA celebrity scene, this is it. The Polo lounge is the restaurant in the Beverly Hilton and is prototypical Beverly Hills. Great service and they even had a one man xmas band entertaining during dinner. The food was excellent and the sommelier Nino had an encyclopedic knowledge of California wines. I highly recommend the Smoked Balik Salmon, it's unbelievable and the best salmon I've ever had. The oysters on ice are great but I'm not much for Oyster shooters personally. When it comes to entrees, get the Pappardelle, it was delicious. Literally, lick the plate savory sauce, it took all my will power to hold back. For the close, I took advantage of the deconstructed s'mores which was great but not quite the same caliber as the salmon or pappardelle. Rumor has it that this place is even better for brunch, I'm definitely going back.< /Text>< pictures>

<user_id>104453286420785430779< /user_id>< text>
David here,

Over the last decade I have been looking at the skeletal remains of my once proud skateboard, constantly telling myself to fix it up and get back to the sport I once loved so well. So today I did it, went into Street Science for a whole new setup, right off the bat MacKenzie welcomed me in and started guiding my way through the new brands.

I was amazed to find out all of my tried and true brands were dust in the wind, sold out to walmart and suffered huge reduction in quality, but MacKenzie was a big help in finding me the right deck for me (I felt bad because she took down about 15 and had to put them back up). In the end I got a really nice finished product that I look forward to testing on the streets. Still the same prices I grew to expect years ago which was a big plus. Awesome time today and I will be coming back for sure.

P.S. they give half pipe/vert lessons starting at $40 which is great for kids.</text>

< Review>
I first want to say that the ladies in the front were very helpful and kind.  This is why I even gave it a 3 star.  I waited over an hour and a half before even getting to see the doctor.  I was very patient and when I asked about the long wait the receptionist brought my 3 year old something to color with.  The lady who took the xrays was really good with my kids too.  The doctor was with us for 60 seconds! He spent no time with us at all.  Then when the lady was cleaning my son's teeth my daughter was asking to sit down because she was tired (we had been there for two hours at this point) and I was holding a chair for her to get up into so she could sit down.  The doctor came over rudely and told me I had to go into the waiting room with my daughter until my son was done.  First of all, I will not be leaving my son! This is why I come here because everything is open and I have always been allowed to stay with my kids the entire time.  Then, he says she couldn't sit so I took her off the seat and pushed the chair towards him and said fine.  He got mad at me because I'm sure I was frustrated at this point.  I told him how I have been very patient at this point and didn't deserve this type of service.  He says "we are trying to help your kids" and he also said "what if she falls?"  I told him that I am a mom if 5 and I know how to take care of my kids.  Remember that I was holding the chair and standing right next to my child when she was trying to sit down! He insisted on me waiting in the waiting room and I refused.  I gave him his chair and stood there until my son was done.  It isn't the fact that she couldn't sit in the chair so much as the way he talked to me.  I am clearly not an ignorant women without common sense.
